<p>The <b>Brazilian Navy</b> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <span lang="pt"><i>Marinha do Brasil</i></span>) is the <a href="/wiki/Navy" title="Navy">naval</a> service branch of the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Armed_Forces" title="Brazilian Armed Forces">Brazilian Armed Forces</a>, responsible for conducting <a href="/wiki/Naval_warfare" title="Naval warfare">naval operations</a>. The Brazilian Navy is the largest navy in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> and in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, and the second largest navy in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>, after the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>The navy was involved in <a href="/wiki/War_of_Independence_of_Brazil#Naval_action" title="War of Independence of Brazil">Brazil's war of independence from Portugal</a>. Most of <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>'s naval forces and bases in South America were transferred to the newly independent country. In the initial decades following independence, the country maintained a large naval force and the navy was later involved in the <a href="/wiki/Cisplatine_War" title="Cisplatine War">Cisplatine War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_conflicts_in_South_America" title="List of conflicts in South America">River Plate conflicts</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_War" title="Paraguayan War">Paraguayan War</a> as well as other sporadic <a href="/wiki/List_of_conflicts_in_South_America" title="List of conflicts in South America">rebellions</a> that marked Brazilian history.</p>
<p>By the 1880s the Brazilian Imperial Navy was the most powerful in South America. After the <a href="/wiki/Revolta_da_Armada" title="Revolta da Armada">1893 naval rebellion</a>, there was a hiatus in the development of the navy until 1905, when Brazil acquired <a href="/wiki/Minas_Geraes-class_battleship" title="Minas Geraes-class battleship">two of the most powerful</a> and advanced <a href="/wiki/Dreadnought" title="Dreadnought">dreadnoughts</a> of the day which sparked <a href="/wiki/South_American_dreadnought_race" title="South American dreadnought race">dreadnought race with Brazil's South American neighbours</a>. The Brazilian Navy participated in both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazil_and_World_War_I" title="Brazil and World War I">World War I</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_Expeditionary_Force_(FEB)" title="Brazilian Expeditionary Force (FEB)">World War II</a>, engaging in anti-submarine patrols in the Atlantic.</p>
<p>The Brazilian Navy's tonnage consists of British-built guided missile <a href="/wiki/Frigate" title="Frigate">frigates</a> (FFG), locally built <a href="/wiki/Corvette" title="Corvette">corvettes</a> (FFL), coastal diesel-electric <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submarines</a> (SSK) and many other river and coastal patrol craft, among other vehicles.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mission">Mission</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Mission">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In addition to the roles of a traditional <a href="/wiki/Navy" title="Navy">navy</a>, the Brazilian Navy also carries out the role of organizing the <a href="/wiki/Merchant_navy" title="Merchant navy">merchant navy</a> and other operational safety missions traditionally conducted by a <a href="/wiki/Coast_guard" title="Coast guard">coast guard</a>. Other roles include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Conducting national maritime policy</li>
<li>Implementing and enforcing laws and regulations with respect to the sea and inland waters.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marquis_of_tamandare_1873.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2076" data-file-width="1216" height="341" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Marquis_of_tamandare_1873.jpg/200px-Marquis_of_tamandare_1873.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Marquis_of_tamandare_1873.jpg/300px-Marquis_of_tamandare_1873.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Marquis_of_tamandare_1873.jpg/400px-Marquis_of_tamandare_1873.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Marquis_of_tamandare_1873.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Patron of the Brazilian Navy <a href="/wiki/Joaquim_Marques_Lisboa,_Marquis_of_Tamandar%C3%A9" title="Joaquim Marques Lisboa, Marquis of Tamandaré">Joaquim Marques Lisboa, Marquis of Tamandaré</a>, in 1873.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The origins of the Brazilian Navy date back to the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Navy" title="Portuguese Navy">Portuguese naval forces</a> based in Brazil. The transfer of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Portuguese monarchy</a> to Brazil in 1808 during the Napoleonic wars also resulted in the transfer of a large part of the structure, personnel and ships of the Portuguese Navy. These became the core of the Navy of Brazil.</p>
<h3><span id="Imperial_Navy_(1822–1889)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Imperial_Navy_.281822.E2.80.931889.29">Imperial Navy (1822–1889)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Imperial Navy (1822–1889)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Brazilian_Navy" title="Imperial Brazilian Navy">Imperial Brazilian Navy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Treino_da_armada_brasileira_1870.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="849" data-file-width="1831" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Treino_da_armada_brasileira_1870.jpg/400px-Treino_da_armada_brasileira_1870.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Treino_da_armada_brasileira_1870.jpg/600px-Treino_da_armada_brasileira_1870.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Treino_da_armada_brasileira_1870.jpg/800px-Treino_da_armada_brasileira_1870.jpg 2x" width="400"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Treino_da_armada_brasileira_1870.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ships of the Imperial Navy in training, <a href="/wiki/Guanabara_Bay" title="Guanabara Bay">Guanabara Bay</a>, Rio de Janeiro, 1870s.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="War_of_Independence">War of Independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: War of Independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Brazil#Independence_War" title="Independence of Brazil">Independence of Brazil § Independence War</a></div>
<p>The Brazilian Navy came into being with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Brazilian Declaration of Independence">independence of the country</a>. Some of its members were native-born Brazilians, who under Portuguese rule had been forbidden to serve, while other members were Portuguese born who adhered to the cause of independence and foreign mercenaries. A number of establishments previously created by King <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_VI_of_Portugal" title="João VI of Portugal">João VI of Portugal</a> were incorporated into the navy such as the Department of Navy, Headquarters of the Navy, the Intendancy and Accounting Department, the Arsenal (Shipyard) of the Navy, the Academy of Navy Guards, the Naval Hospital, the Auditorship, the Supreme Military Council, the powder plant, and others. The Brazilian-born Captain <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lu%C3%ADs_da_Cunha_Moreira&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Luís da Cunha Moreira (page does not exist)">Luís da Cunha Moreira</a> was chosen as the first minister of the Navy on 28 October 1822.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolanda1974260_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolanda1974260-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaia197553_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaia197553-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>British naval officer <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cochrane,_10th_Earl_of_Dundonald" title="Thomas Cochrane, 10th Earl of Dundonald">Lord Thomas Alexander Cochrane</a> was made the commander of the Brazilian Navy and received the rank of "First Admiral".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaia197558.E2.80.9361_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaia197558.E2.80.9361-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolanda1974261_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolanda1974261-6">[6]</a></sup> At that time, the fleet was composed of one <a href="/wiki/Ship_of_the_line" title="Ship of the line">ship of the line</a>, four <a href="/wiki/Frigate" title="Frigate">frigates</a>, and smaller ships for a total of 38 <a href="/wiki/Warship" title="Warship">warships</a>. The Secretary of Treasury <a href="/wiki/Martim_Francisco_Ribeiro_de_Andrada" title="Martim Francisco Ribeiro de Andrada">Martim Francisco Ribeiro de Andrada</a> created a national subscription to generate capital in order to increase the size of the fleet. Contributions were sent from all over Brazil. Even <a href="/wiki/Pedro_I_of_Brazil" title="Pedro I of Brazil">Emperor Pedro I</a> acquired a merchant <a href="/wiki/Brig" title="Brig">brig</a> at his own expense (renamed <i>Caboclo</i>) and donated it to the Navy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolanda1974261_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolanda1974261-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaia197554.E2.80.9357_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaia197554.E2.80.9357-7">[7]</a></sup> The navy fought in the north and also south of Brazil where it had a decisive role in the independence of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolanda1974272_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolanda1974272-8">[8]</a></sup> After the suppression of the <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_the_Equator" title="Confederation of the Equator">revolt in Pernambuco</a> in 1824 and prior to the <a href="/wiki/Cisplatine_War" title="Cisplatine War">Cisplatine War</a>, the navy increased significantly in size and strength. Starting with 38 ships in 1822, eventually the navy had 96 modern warships of various types with over 690 cannon.</p>
<h4><span id="Cisplatine_War_and_rebellions_(1825–1849)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Cisplatine_War_and_rebellions_.281825.E2.80.931849.29">Cisplatine War and rebellions (1825–1849)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Cisplatine War and rebellions (1825–1849)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cisplatine_War" title="Cisplatine War">Cisplatine War</a></div>
<p><br/></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<p>Example of vessels commissioned during this period:</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 90.666666666667px">
<div style="width: 90.666666666667px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 88.666666666667px;">
<div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bertioga.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="302" data-file-width="223" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Bertioga.png/133px-Bertioga.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Bertioga.png/199px-Bertioga.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2f/Bertioga.png 2x" width="89"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Escuna <i>Bertioga</i>, 1825</p>
</div>
</div>
</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 143.33333333333px">
<div style="width: 143.33333333333px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 141.33333333333px;">
<div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fregata_Amalia.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="832" data-file-width="978" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Fregata_Amalia.jpg/212px-Fregata_Amalia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Fregata_Amalia.jpg/317px-Fregata_Amalia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Fregata_Amalia.jpg/423px-Fregata_Amalia.jpg 2x" width="142"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Frigate <i>Amalia</i>, 1843</p>
</div>
</div>
</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 244px">
<div style="width: 244px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 242px;">
<div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Steamship_dom_Afonso.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="848" data-file-width="1706" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Steamship_dom_Afonso.jpg/363px-Steamship_dom_Afonso.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Steamship_dom_Afonso.jpg/544px-Steamship_dom_Afonso.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Steamship_dom_Afonso.jpg/725px-Steamship_dom_Afonso.jpg 2x" width="242"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Steam corvette <i>Dom Afonso</i>, 1850</p>
</div>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The Navy blocked the estuary of the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata" title="Río de la Plata">Río de la Plata</a> hindering the contact of the United Provinces (as Argentina was then called) with the Cisplatine rebels who wanted Uruguay to joined Argentina again or become an independent country, and the outside world. Several battles had occurred between Brazilian and Argentine ships until the defeat of an Argentine flotilla composed of two <a href="/wiki/Corvette" title="Corvette">corvettes</a>, five brigs and one <a href="/wiki/Barquentine" title="Barquentine">barquentine</a> near the Island of Santiago in 1827. The war came to a draw and in 1828 had to accept the independence of Uruguay. When Pedro I abdicated in 1831, he left a powerful navy made up of two ships of the line and ten <a href="/wiki/Frigate" title="Frigate">frigates</a> in addition to corvettes, <a href="/wiki/Steamship" title="Steamship">steamships</a>, and other ships for a total of at least 80 warships in peace time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaia1975133.E2.80.9335_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaia1975133.E2.80.9335-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolanda264_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolanda264-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 58-year reign of <a href="/wiki/Pedro_II_of_Brazil" title="Pedro II of Brazil">Pedro II</a> the Brazilian Navy achieved its greatest strength in relation to navies around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaia1975216_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaia1975216-11">[11]</a></sup> The Arsenal, Navy department, and the Naval Jail were improved and the Imperial Marine Corps was created. Steam navigation was adopted. Brazil quickly modernized its fleet acquiring ships from foreign sources while also constructing ships locally. Brazil's Navy substituted the old <a href="/wiki/Smoothbore" title="Smoothbore">smoothbore</a> cannon for new ones with rifled barrels, which were more accurate and had longer ranges. Improvements were also made in the Arsenals (shipyards) and naval bases, which were equipped with new workshops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolanda1974264_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolanda1974264-12">[12]</a></sup> Ships were constructed in the Naval Arsenal of Rio de Janeiro, Salvador, Recife, Santos, Niterói and Pelotas. The Navy also successfully fought against all revolts that occurred during the Regency where it conducted blockades and transported the Army troops; including Cabanagem, <a href="/wiki/Ragamuffin_War" title="Ragamuffin War">Ragamuffin War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sabinada" title="Sabinada">Sabinada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Balaiada" title="Balaiada">Balaiada</a>, amongst others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolanda1974264_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolanda1974264-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaia1975205.E2.80.936_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaia1975205.E2.80.936-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>When Emperor Pedro II was declared of legal age and assumed his constitutional prerogatives in 1840, the Armada had over 90 warships: six frigates, seven corvettes, two barque-schooners, six brigs, eight brig-schooners, 16 <a href="/wiki/Gunboat" title="Gunboat">gunboats</a>, 12 schooners, seven armed brigantine-schooners, six steam <a href="/wiki/Barque" title="Barque">barques</a>, three transport ships, two armed <a href="/wiki/Lugger" title="Lugger">luggers</a>, two <a href="/wiki/Cutter_(boat)" title="Cutter (boat)">cutters</a> and thirteen larger <a href="/wiki/Boat" title="Boat">boats</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaia1975210_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaia1975210-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 1850s the State Secretary, the Accounting Department of the Navy, the Headquarters of the Navy and the Naval Academy were reorganized and improved. New ships were purchased and the ports administrations were better equipped. The Imperial Mariner Corps was definitively regularized and the Marine Corps was created, taking the place of the Naval Artillery. The Service of Assistance for Invalids was also established, along with several schools for sailors and craftsmen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJanotti1986207.E2.80.938_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJanotti1986207.E2.80.938-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span id="Platine_&amp;_Paraguayan_wars_(1849–1870)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Platine_.26_Paraguayan_wars_.281849.E2.80.931870.29">Platine &amp; Paraguayan wars (1849–1870)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Platine &amp; Paraguayan wars (1849–1870)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_War" title="Paraguayan War">Paraguayan War</a></div>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

</div>
</div>
<p>The conflicts in the Platine region did not cease after the war of 1825. The anarchy caused by the despotic Rosas and his desire to subdue Bolívia, Uruguay and Paraguay <a href="/wiki/Platine_War" title="Platine War">forced Brazil to intercede</a>. The Brazilian Government sent a naval force of 17 warships (a ship of the line, 10 corvettes and six steamships) commanded by the veteran John Pascoe Grenfell.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolanda1974265_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolanda1974265-16">[16]</a></sup> The Brazilian fleet <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Passage_of_the_Tonelero" title="Passage of the Tonelero">succeeded in passing</a> through the Argentine line of defence at the Tonelero Pass under heavy attack and transported the troops to the theater of operations. The Brazilian Armada had a total of 59 vessels of various types in 1851: 36 armed sailing ships, 10 armed steamships, seven unarmed sailing ships and six sailing transports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarvalho1975181_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarvalho1975181-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>More than a decade later the Armada was once again modernized and its fleet of old sailing ships was converted to a fleet of 40 steamships armed with more than 250 cannons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolanda1974266_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolanda1974266-18">[18]</a></sup> In 1864 the navy fought in the <a href="/wiki/Uruguayan_War" title="Uruguayan War">Uruguayan War</a> and immediately afterwards in the <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_War" title="Paraguayan War">Paraguayan War</a> where it annihilated the Paraguayan navy in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Riachuelo" title="Battle of Riachuelo">Battle of Riachuelo</a>. The navy was further augmented with the acquisition of 20 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ironclad" title="Ironclad">ironclads</a> and six fluvial <a href="/wiki/Monitor_(warship)" title="Monitor (warship)">monitors</a>. At least 9,177 navy personnel fought in the five years' conflict.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESalles200338_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESalles200338-19">[19]</a></sup> Brazilian naval constructors such as Napoleão Level, Trajano de Carvalho and João Cândido Brasil planned new concepts for warships that allowed the country's Arsenals to retain their competitiveness with other nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaia1975219_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaia1975219-20">[20]</a></sup> All damage suffered by ships was repaired and various improvements were made to them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJanotti1986208_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJanotti1986208-21">[21]</a></sup> In 1870, Brazil had 94 modern warships<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchwarcz2002305_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchwarcz2002305-22">[22]</a></sup> and had the fifth most powerful navy in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoratioto199623_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoratioto199623-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span id="Expansion_and_the_end_of_the_Empire_(1870–1889)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion_and_the_end_of_the_Empire_.281870.E2.80.931889.29">Expansion and the end of the Empire (1870–1889)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Expansion and the end of the Empire (1870–1889)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cruzador_Pereira_da_Cunha.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="451" data-file-width="640" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Cruzador_Pereira_da_Cunha.jpg/256px-Cruzador_Pereira_da_Cunha.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Cruzador_Pereira_da_Cunha.jpg/383px-Cruzador_Pereira_da_Cunha.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Cruzador_Pereira_da_Cunha.jpg/511px-Cruzador_Pereira_da_Cunha.jpg 2x" width="171"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="gallerytext">

</div>
</div>
</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 156.66666666667px">
<div style="width: 156.66666666667px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 154.66666666667px;">
<div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tiradentes,_Brazil_(14868394958).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="776" data-file-width="1000" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Tiradentes%2C_Brazil_%2814868394958%29.jpg/232px-Tiradentes%2C_Brazil_%2814868394958%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Tiradentes%2C_Brazil_%2814868394958%29.jpg/348px-Tiradentes%2C_Brazil_%2814868394958%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Tiradentes%2C_Brazil_%2814868394958%29.jpg/464px-Tiradentes%2C_Brazil_%2814868394958%29.jpg 2x" width="155"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Torpedo boat <i>Tiradentes</i>, 1893.</p>
</div>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
<p>During the 1870s, the Brazilian Government strengthened the navy as the possibility of a war against Argentina over Paraguay's future became quite real. Thus, it acquired a <a href="/wiki/Gunboat" title="Gunboat">gunboat</a> and a corvette in 1873; an ironclad and a monitor in 1874; and immediately afterwards two <a href="/wiki/Cruiser" title="Cruiser">cruisers</a> and another monitor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolanda1974272_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolanda1974272-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoratioto2002466_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoratioto2002466-24">[24]</a></sup> The improvement of the Armada continued during the 1880s. The Arsenals of the Navy in the provinces of Rio de Janeiro, Bahia, Pernambuco, Pará and Mato Grosso continued to build dozens of warships. Also, four torpedo boats were purchased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaia1975225_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaia1975225-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cruzador_Almirante_Barroso_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="675" data-file-width="559" height="266" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Cruzador_Almirante_Barroso_1.jpg/220px-Cruzador_Almirante_Barroso_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Cruzador_Almirante_Barroso_1.jpg/330px-Cruzador_Almirante_Barroso_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Cruzador_Almirante_Barroso_1.jpg/440px-Cruzador_Almirante_Barroso_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cruzador_Almirante_Barroso_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cruiser <i>Almirante Barroso</i>, 1880.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On November 30, 1883, the Practical School of Torpedoes was created along with a workshop devoted to constructing and repairing torpedoes and electric devices in the Arsenal of Navy of Rio de Janeiro.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaia1975221_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaia1975221-26">[26]</a></sup> This Arsenal constructed four steam gunboats and one schooner, all with iron and steel hulls (the first of these categories constructed in the country).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaia1975225_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaia1975225-25">[25]</a></sup> The Imperial Armada reached its apex with the incorporation of the ironclad <a href="/wiki/Battleship" title="Battleship">battleships</a> <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_battleship_Riachuelo" title="Brazilian battleship Riachuelo"><i>Riachuelo</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_battleship_Aquidab%C3%A3" title="Brazilian battleship Aquidabã"><i>Aquidabã</i></a> (both equipped with torpedo launchers) in 1884 and 1885, respectively. Both ships (considered state-of-the-art by experts from Europe) allowed the Brazilian Armada to retain its position as one of the most powerful naval forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaia1975221.2C_227_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaia1975221.2C_227-27">[27]</a></sup> By 1889, the navy had 60 warships<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJanotti1986208_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJanotti1986208-21">[21]</a></sup> and was the fifth or sixth most powerful navy in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalmon2002265_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalmon2002265-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the last cabinet of the monarchic regime, the Minister of the Navy, Admiral <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_da_Costa_Azevedo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="José da Costa Azevedo (page does not exist)">José da Costa Azevedo</a> (the Baron of Ladário), left the reorganization and modernization of the navy unfinished.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJanotti1986208_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJanotti1986208-21">[21]</a></sup> The coup that ended the monarchy in Brazil in 1889 was not well accepted by the Armada. Imperial Mariners were attacked when they tried to support the imprisoned Emperor in the City Palace. The Marquis of Tamandaré begged Pedro II to allow him to fight back the coup; however, the Emperor refused to allow any bloodshed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalmon19751603_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalmon19751603-29">[29]</a></sup> Tamandaré would later be imprisoned by order of the dictator <a href="/wiki/Floriano_Peixoto" title="Floriano Peixoto">Floriano Peixoto</a> under the accusation of financing the monarchist military in the Federalist Revolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJanotti198666_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJanotti198666-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Baron of Ladário remained in contact with the exiled Imperial Family, hoping to restore the monarchy, but ended up ostracized by the republican government. Admiral Saldanha da Gama led the <a href="/wiki/Revolta_da_Armada" title="Revolta da Armada">Revolt of the Armada</a> with the objective of restoring the Empire and allied himself with other monarchists who were fighting in the Federalist Revolution. However, all the attempts at restoration were violently crushed. High-ranking Monarchist officers were imprisoned, banished or executed by firing squad without due process of law and their subordinates also suffered harsh punishments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJanotti1986209_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJanotti1986209-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Early_republic_(1889–1917)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_republic_.281889.E2.80.931917.29">Early republic (1889–1917)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Early republic (1889–1917)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Naval_revolts">Naval revolts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Naval revolts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Revolta_da_Armada" title="Revolta da Armada">Revolta da Armada</a></div>
<p>The military coup that led to the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil#Fall" title="Empire of Brazil">proclamation of the Brazilian Republic</a> (1889), accentuated the decline of shipbuilding in the country. For four decades, between 1890 and 1930 no new ships were built in Brazil. The focus of republican governments was to equip the army to fight internal uprisings in the new regime's early years. The Navy was perceived as a threat to the new republican regime, as it had been more loyal to the Monarchy.</p>
<p>The situation became precarious in just over a decade as the Naval Battalion was reduced to 295 soldiers and Imperial Marines to 1,904 men. The equipment and vessels acquired were considered outdated by Navy officials, who criticized the abandonment of repair shops. Naval officers participated in two riots, known as <a href="/wiki/Revolta_da_Armada" title="Revolta da Armada">Naval Riots</a>. The second, avowedly monarchist, cost the officers their careers and their lives, without entering the military justice process. The sailors who obeyed orders and took part in the attempt to restore monarchy suffered cruelly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJanotti1986_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJanotti1986-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (January 2014)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="South_American_naval_rivalry">South American naval rivalry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: South American naval rivalry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/South_American_dreadnought_race" title="South American dreadnought race">South American dreadnought race</a></div>

<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brazilian_battleship_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_trials.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Battleship <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_battleship_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Brazilian battleship São Paulo"><i>São Paulo</i></a> (1910–1951).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brazil's navy fell into disrepair and obsolescence in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Decline_and_fall_of_Pedro_II_of_Brazil#Fall" title="Decline and fall of Pedro II of Brazil">1889 revolution</a>, which deposed <a href="/wiki/List_of_monarchs_of_Brazil" title="List of monarchs of Brazil">Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Pedro_II_of_Brazil" title="Pedro II of Brazil">Pedro II</a>, after naval officers led a <a href="/wiki/Revolta_da_Armada" title="Revolta da Armada">revolt in 1893–94</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Meanwhile, although the Argentine–Chilean agreement had limited their naval expansion, they still retained the numerous vessels built in the interim,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> so around the start of the 20th century the Brazilian Navy lagged far behind its Argentine and Chilean counterparts in quality and total tonnage,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> despite Brazil having nearly three times the population of Argentina and almost five times that of Chile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The navy had just forty-five percent of its authorized personnel in 1896, and the only modern armored ships were two small coast-defense vessels launched in 1898.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)#Early_20th_century" title="São Paulo (state)">Rising demand for coffee</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rubber_boom" title="Rubber boom">rubber brought Brazil an influx of revenue</a> in the early 1900s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Simultaneously, there was a drive on the part of prominent Brazilians, most notably <a href="/wiki/Pinheiro_Machado_(politician)" title="Pinheiro Machado (politician)">Pinheiro Machado</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Paranhos,_Baron_of_Rio_Branco" title="José Paranhos, Baron of Rio Branco">Baron of Rio Branco</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[A]</a></sup> to have the country recognized as an international power. A strong navy was seen as crucial to this goal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Brazil" title="National Congress of Brazil">National Congress of Brazil</a> drew up and passed a large naval acquisition program in late 1904, but it was two years before any ships were ordered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>Law no. 1452 was passed on 30 December 1905, which authorized £4,214,550 for new warship construction, £1,685,820 in 1906, three small battleships, three <a href="/wiki/Armored_cruiser" title="Armored cruiser">armored cruisers</a>, six <a href="/wiki/Destroyer" title="Destroyer">destroyers</a>, twelve <a href="/wiki/Torpedo_boat" title="Torpedo boat">torpedo boats</a>, three <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submarines</a>, and two <a href="/wiki/River_monitor" title="River monitor">river monitors</a> were ordered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup> Though the Brazilian government later eliminated the armored cruisers for reasons of cost, the Minister of the Navy, Admiral <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BAlio_C%C3%A9sar_de_Noronha" title="Júlio César de Noronha">Júlio César de Noronha</a>, signed a contract with Armstrong Whitworth for three small battleships on 23 July 1906.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>British shipyards were ordered to build two <a href="/wiki/Dreadnought" title="Dreadnought">dreadnought</a> battleships, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_battleship_Minas_Gerais" title="Brazilian battleship Minas Gerais"><i>Minas Gerais</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_battleship_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Brazilian battleship São Paulo"><i>São Paulo</i></a>; this started a naval arms race with Argentina and Chile. Later <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_battleship_Rio_de_Janeiro_(1913)" title="Brazilian battleship Rio de Janeiro (1913)"><i>Rio de Janeiro</i></a> was ordered and sold and another <i>Riachuelo</i> was never completed as a result of the First World War.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Revolt_of_the_Lash">Revolt of the Lash</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Revolt of the Lash">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Joao_Candido.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="595" data-file-width="971" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Joao_Candido.jpg/240px-Joao_Candido.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Joao_Candido.jpg/360px-Joao_Candido.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Joao_Candido.jpg/480px-Joao_Candido.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Joao_Candido.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_C%C3%A2ndido_Felisberto" title="João Cândido Felisberto">João Cândido Felisberto</a> with reporters, officers and sailors on board <i>Minas Geraes</i> on 26 November 1910, the last day of the Revolt of the Lash</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Revolt_of_the_Lash" title="Revolt of the Lash">Revolt of the Lash</a></div>
<p>Soon after <i>São Paulo</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s arrival, a major rebellion known as the Revolt of the Lash, or <i>Revolta da Chibata</i>, broke out on four of the newest ships in the Brazilian Navy. The initial spark was provided on 21 November 1910 when <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afro-Brazilian" title="Afro-Brazilian">Afro-Brazilian</a> sailor <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Marcelino_Rodrigues_Menezes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Marcelino Rodrigues Menezes (page does not exist)">Marcelino Rodrigues Menezes</a> was brutally flogged 250 times for insubordination. Many Afro-Brazilian sailors were sons of former slaves, or were former slaves freed under the <i><a href="/wiki/Lei_%C3%81urea" title="Lei Áurea">Lei Áurea</a></i> (abolition) but forced to enter the navy. They had been planning a revolt for some time, and Menezes became the catalyst. Further preparations were needed, so the rebellion was delayed until 22 November. The crewmen of <i>Minas Geraes</i>, <i>São Paulo</i>, the twelve-year-old <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_battleship_Deodoro" title="Brazilian battleship Deodoro"><i>Deodoro</i></a>, and the new <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_cruiser_Bahia" title="Brazilian cruiser Bahia"><i>Bahia</i></a> quickly took their vessels with only a minimum of bloodshed: two officers on <i>Minas Geraes</i> and one each on <i>São Paulo</i> and <i>Bahia</i> were killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>The ships were well-supplied with foodstuffs, ammunition, and coal, and the only demand of mutineers—led by <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_C%C3%A2ndido_Felisberto" title="João Cândido Felisberto">João Cândido Felisberto</a>—was the abolition of "slavery as practiced by the Brazilian Navy". They objected to low pay, long hours, inadequate training for incompetent sailors, and punishments including <i>bôlo</i> (being struck on the hand with a <a href="/wiki/Ferrule" title="Ferrule">ferrule</a>) and the use of whips or lashes (<i>chibata</i>), which eventually became a symbol of the revolt. By 23 November, the National Congress had begun discussing the possibility of a general <a href="/wiki/Amnesty" title="Amnesty">amnesty</a> for the sailors. Senator <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ruy_Barbosa" title="Ruy Barbosa">Ruy Barbosa</a>, long an opponent of slavery, lent a large amount of support, and the measure unanimously passed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Senate_of_Brazil" title="Senate of Brazil">Federal Senate</a> on 24 November. The measure was then sent to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Deputies_of_Brazil" title="Chamber of Deputies of Brazil">Chamber of Deputies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>Humiliated by the revolt, naval officers and the president of Brazil were staunchly opposed to amnesty, so they quickly began planning to assault the rebel ships. The former believed such an action was necessary to restore the service's honor. Late on 24 November, the President ordered the naval officers to attack the mutineers. Officers crewed some smaller warships and the cruiser <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_cruiser_Rio_Grande_do_Sul" title="Brazilian cruiser Rio Grande do Sul"><i>Rio Grande do Sul</i></a>, <i>Bahia</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s <a href="/wiki/Sister_ship" title="Sister ship">sister ship</a> with ten 4.7-inch (119 mm) guns. They planned to attack on the morning of 25 November, when the government expected the mutineers would return to <a href="/wiki/Guanabara_Bay" title="Guanabara Bay">Guanabara Bay</a>. When they did not return and the amnesty measure neared passage in the Chamber of Deputies, the order was rescinded. After the bill passed 125–23 and the president signed it into law, the mutineers stood down on 26 November.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the revolt, the ships were noted by many observers to be well-handled, despite a previous belief that the Brazilian Navy was incapable of effectively operating the ships even before being split by a rebellion.</p>
<h3><span id="World_Wars_(1917–1945)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Wars_.281917.E2.80.931945.29">World Wars (1917–1945)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: World Wars (1917–1945)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h4><span id="First_World_War_(1917–1918)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="First_World_War_.281917.E2.80.931918.29">First World War (1917–1918)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: First World War (1917–1918)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Brazil_during_World_War_I" title="Brazil during World War I">Brazil during World War I</a> and <a href="/wiki/U-boat_Campaign_(World_War_I)" title="U-boat Campaign (World War I)">U-boat Campaign (World War I)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brazilian_Navy_1914.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="746" data-file-width="1295" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Brazilian_Navy_1914.PNG/240px-Brazilian_Navy_1914.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Brazilian_Navy_1914.PNG/360px-Brazilian_Navy_1914.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Brazilian_Navy_1914.PNG/480px-Brazilian_Navy_1914.PNG 2x" width="240"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brazilian_Navy_1914.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Warship silhouettes of the Brazilian Navy, 1914</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the declaration of war on the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a> in October 1917 the Brazilian Navy participated in the war. On 21 December 1917 the British government requested that a Brazilian naval force of light cruisers be placed under Royal Navy control and a squadron comprising the cruisers <i>Rio Grande do Sul</i> and <i>Bahia</i>, the destroyers <i>Paraíba</i>, <i>Rio Grande do Norte</i>, <i>Piauí</i>, and <i>Santa Catarina</i>, and the support ship <i>Belmonte</i> and the ocean-going <a href="/wiki/Tugboat" title="Tugboat">tugboat</a> <i>Laurindo Pitta</i> was formed, designated the <i>Divisão Naval em Operações de Guerra</i> ("Naval Division in <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=War_Operations&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="War Operations (page does not exist)">War Operations</a>"). The DNOG sailed on 31 July 1918 from <a href="/wiki/Fernando_de_Noronha" title="Fernando de Noronha">Fernando de Noronha</a> for <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a>, arriving at <a href="/wiki/Freetown" title="Freetown">Freetown</a> on 9 August, and sailing onwards to its new base of operations, <a href="/wiki/Dakar" title="Dakar">Dakar</a>, on 23 August. On the night of 25 August the division believed it had been attacked by a <a href="/wiki/U-boat" title="U-boat">U-boat</a> when the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Auxiliary_cruiser" title="Auxiliary cruiser">auxiliary cruiser</a> <i>Belmonte</i> sighted a torpedo track. The purported submarine was <a href="/wiki/Depth_charge" title="Depth charge">depth-charged</a>, fired on, and reportedly sunk by <i>Rio Grande do Norte</i>, but the sinking was never confirmed.</p>
<p>The DNOG patrolled the Dakar–<a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a>–<a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> triangle, which was suspected to be used by U-boats waiting on convoys, until 3 November 1918 when it sailed for Gibraltar to begin operations in the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>, with the exception of <i>Rio Grande do Sul</i>, <i>Rio Grande do Norte</i>, and <i>Belmonte</i>. The Division arrived at Gibraltar on 10 November; while passing through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Straits_of_Gibraltar" title="Straits of Gibraltar">Straits of Gibraltar</a>, they mistook three <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subchaser" title="Subchaser">subchasers</a> for U-boats but no damage was caused.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span id="Second_World_War_(1942–1945)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_World_War_.281942.E2.80.931945.29">Second World War (1942–1945)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Second World War (1942–1945)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NHi_Vital_de_Oliveira.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="454" data-file-width="640" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/NHi_Vital_de_Oliveira.jpg/220px-NHi_Vital_de_Oliveira.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/NHi_Vital_de_Oliveira.jpg/330px-NHi_Vital_de_Oliveira.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/NHi_Vital_de_Oliveira.jpg/440px-NHi_Vital_de_Oliveira.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NHi_Vital_de_Oliveira.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Transport <i>Vital de Oliveira</i>, sunk in 1942.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brazilian_cruiser_Bahia_2.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="991" data-file-width="1294" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Brazilian_cruiser_Bahia_2.JPG/220px-Brazilian_cruiser_Bahia_2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Brazilian_cruiser_Bahia_2.JPG/330px-Brazilian_cruiser_Bahia_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Brazilian_cruiser_Bahia_2.JPG/440px-Brazilian_cruiser_Bahia_2.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brazilian_cruiser_Bahia_2.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cruiser <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_cruiser_Bahia" title="Brazilian cruiser Bahia"><i>Bahia</i></a> (1910–1945 sunk by an explosion).</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Atlantic" title="Battle of the Atlantic">Battle of the Atlantic</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazil_during_World_War_II" title="Brazil during World War II">Brazil during World War II</a></div>
<p>Having the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> blocked and the necessity to go beyond to the far East, Germany used the Atlantic Ocean to maintain its supply of material necessities.</p>
<p>In World War II, Brazil's navy was obsolete. In early 1942, German submarines aimed to interdict supplies from reaching Britain and the Soviet Union. Between 1942 and 1944, Brazil's navy was supported by the United States Navy. During this period several naval bases were established in the North and Northeast of Brazil, becoming the headquarters of the Allied Command Atlantic South.</p>
<p>Within their limitations and with the refitting and reorganization promoted with American resources, the Brazilian Navy participated actively in the fight <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-submarine" title="Anti-submarine">against U-boats</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Atlantic" title="South Atlantic">South</a>, Central Atlantic and also the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>. They guarded <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied</a> <a href="/wiki/Convoy" title="Convoy">convoys</a> bound for <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a> and the Mediterranean. Between 1942 and 1945 the navy was responsible for conducting 574 convoy operations protecting 3,164 merchant ships of various nationalities. Enemy submarines managed to sink only three vessels. According to German documentation the Brazilian Navy made over sixty-six attacks against German submarines.</p>
<p>A total of nine U-boats known German submarines were destroyed along the Brazilian coast. Those were: <a href="/wiki/German_submarine_U-164_(1941)" title="German submarine U-164 (1941)"><i>U-164</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/German_submarine_U-128_(1941)" title="German submarine U-128 (1941)"><i>U-128</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/German_submarine_U-590" title="German submarine U-590"><i>U-590</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/German_submarine_U-513" title="German submarine U-513"><i>U-513</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/German_submarine_U-662" title="German submarine U-662"><i>U-662</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/German_submarine_U-598" title="German submarine U-598"><i>U-598</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/German_submarine_U-199" title="German submarine U-199"><i>U-199</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/German_submarine_U-591" title="German submarine U-591"><i>U-591</i></a>, and <a href="/wiki/German_submarine_U-161_(1941)" title="German submarine U-161 (1941)"><i>U-161</i></a></p>
<p>About 1,100 Brazilians died during the Battle of the Atlantic as a result of the sinking of 32 Brazilian merchant vessels and a naval warship. Among the 972 dead from the merchant vessels, 470 were crew and 502 were civilian passengers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> Besides these, 99 sailors died in the sinking of <i>Vital de Oliveira</i> when she was attacked by German submarines, in addition to some 350 deaths in accidents that resulted in the sinking of the corvette <i>Camaquã</i> on 21 July 1944. The cruiser <i>Bahia</i> was sunk by an explosion on 4 July 1945 which resulted in the deaths of over 300 men.</p>
<h3><span id="Cold_War_period_(1945–2000)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Cold_War_period_.281945.E2.80.932000.29">Cold War period (1945–2000)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Cold War period (1945–2000)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h4><span id="Lobster_War_(1961–1963)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Lobster_War_.281961.E2.80.931963.29">Lobster War (1961–1963)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Lobster War (1961–1963)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Lobster_War" title="Lobster War">Lobster War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brazil%E2%80%93France_relations" title="Brazil–France relations">Brazil–France relations</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brazilian_cruiser_Tamandar%C3%A9_(C12)_underway_with_destroyers_during_the_1961_Lobster_War.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2006" data-file-width="2744" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Brazilian_cruiser_Tamandar%C3%A9_%28C12%29_underway_with_destroyers_during_the_1961_Lobster_War.jpg/200px-Brazilian_cruiser_Tamandar%C3%A9_%28C12%29_underway_with_destroyers_during_the_1961_Lobster_War.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Brazilian_cruiser_Tamandar%C3%A9_%28C12%29_underway_with_destroyers_during_the_1961_Lobster_War.jpg/300px-Brazilian_cruiser_Tamandar%C3%A9_%28C12%29_underway_with_destroyers_during_the_1961_Lobster_War.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Brazilian_cruiser_Tamandar%C3%A9_%28C12%29_underway_with_destroyers_during_the_1961_Lobster_War.jpg/400px-Brazilian_cruiser_Tamandar%C3%A9_%28C12%29_underway_with_destroyers_during_the_1961_Lobster_War.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brazilian_cruiser_Tamandar%C3%A9_(C12)_underway_with_destroyers_during_the_1961_Lobster_War.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Brazilian Navy in <a href="/wiki/Lobster_War" title="Lobster War">Lobster War</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1961, some groups of French fishermen who were operating very profitably off the coast of Mauritania extended their search to the other side of the Atlantic Ocean, settling on a spot off the coast of Brazil where lobsters are found on submerged ledges at depths of 250–650 ft (76–198 m). Local fishermen complained that large boats were coming from France to catch lobster off the state of Pernambuco, so the Brazilian Admiral Arnoldo Toscano ordered two corvettes to sail to the area where the French fishing boats were located. Seeing that the fishermen's claim was justifiable, the captain of the Brazilian vessel then demanded that the French boats retreat to deeper water, leaving the continental shelf to smaller Brazilian vessels. The situation became very tense once the French rejected this demand and radioed a message asking for the French government to send a destroyer to accompany the lobster boats, which prompted the Brazilian government to put fleet in a state of alert.</p>
<p>The French Government dispatched a <a href="/wiki/T_53-class_destroyer" title="T 53-class destroyer">T 53-class</a> destroyer on 21 February to watch over the French fishing boats. The French vessel withdrew after the arrival of a Brazilian warship and the aircraft carrier <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_aircraft_carrier_Minas_Gerais" title="Brazilian aircraft carrier Minas Gerais"><i>Minas Gerais</i></a>.</p>
<h4><span id="1964_coup_d'état"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1964_coup_d.27.C3.A9tat">1964 coup d'état</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: 1964 coup d'état">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Although corporal punishment was officially abolished after the Revolt of the Lash, or Revolta da Chibata, at the end of 1910, improvement in working conditions and career plans were still contentious in early 1960. The dissatisfaction with officialdom and conservative politicians, coupled with the lack of vision and inability of the general policy of then president <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Goulart" title="João Goulart">João Goulart</a>, led the sailors, encouraged by leaders such as Corporal Anselmo, to the military coup of 1964.</p>
<p>The purges carried out later (not just the navy but for all the armed forces), and the establishment of certain criteria for selection of its new members were a military term in the Brazilian tradition among its members openly harboring various currents of political thought.</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colossus-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Colossus-class aircraft carrier"><i>Colossus</i>-class</a> aircraft carrier <i>Minas Gerais</i> served the Navy until its decommissioning in 2001.</p>
<p>The carrier was commissioned as NAeL <i>Minas Gerais</i> (named for Kubitschek's home state) on 6 December 1960. She departed <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a> for Rio de Janeiro on 13 January 1961. The duration of the refit meant that while the carrier was the first purchased by a Latin American nation, she was the second to enter service, after another <i>Colossus</i>-class carrier entered service with the <a href="/wiki/Argentine_Navy" title="Argentine Navy">Argentine Navy</a> as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ARA_Independencia_(V-1)" title="ARA Independencia (V-1)">ARA <i>Independencia</i></a> in July 1959.</p>
<h3><span id="Peacekeeping_operations_(2004–present)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Peacekeeping_operations_.282004.E2.80.93present.29">Peacekeeping operations (2004–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Peacekeeping operations (2004–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Haiti">Haiti</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Haiti">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 28 May 2004 four Brazilian Navy ships (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_landing_ship_Mattoso_Maia_(G28)" title="Brazilian landing ship Mattoso Maia (G28)"><i>Mattoso Maia</i></a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_landing_ship_Rio_de_Janeiro_(G31)" title="Brazilian landing ship Rio de Janeiro (G31)"><i>Rio de Janeiro</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_tanker_Almirante_Gast%C3%A3o_Motta_(G23)" title="Brazilian tanker Almirante Gastão Motta (G23)"><i>Almirante Gastão Motta</i></a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_frigate_Bos%C3%ADsio_(F48)" title="Brazilian frigate Bosísio (F48)"><i>Bosísio</i></a>) departed from Rio de Janeiro bound for <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> on a peace mission coordinated by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> (UN). The ships transported part of the military contingent that was involved in Haitian reconstruction. In addition to 150 Marines and Army troops, the ships carried most of the materiel for the Brazilian stabilization force — approximately 120 vehicles, 26 trailers of various types, and 81 containers loaded with equipment and supplies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup> On February 28, 2010, the Brazilian Navy ship <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_landing_ship_Garcia_D%27Avila_(G29)" title="Brazilian landing ship Garcia D'Avila (G29)"><i>Garcia D'Avila</i></a> sailed from Rio de Janeiro with 900 tons of cargo, including humanitarian aid supplies to <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">earthquake victims in Haiti</a> as well as equipment for the Brazilian military that operates in that country.</p>
<p>Ammunition was brought for Brazilian soldiers in addition to 14 power generators and 30 vehicles, including trucks, ambulances and armored vehicles. The ship's crew consisted of 350 mariners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Lebanon">Lebanon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Lebanon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:F_Uni%C3%A3o_(F-45).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="433" data-file-width="640" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/F_Uni%C3%A3o_%28F-45%29.jpg/220px-F_Uni%C3%A3o_%28F-45%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/F_Uni%C3%A3o_%28F-45%29.jpg/330px-F_Uni%C3%A3o_%28F-45%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/F_Uni%C3%A3o_%28F-45%29.jpg/440px-F_Uni%C3%A3o_%28F-45%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:F_Uni%C3%A3o_(F-45).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Frigate <i>União</i>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 15 February 2011, Brazil assumed command of the Maritime Task Force (MTF) of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Interim_Force_in_Lebanon" title="United Nations Interim Force in Lebanon">United Nations Interim Force in Lebanon</a> (UNIFIL).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup> On 4 October the Brazilian Ministries of Defence and Foreign Relations informed authorities that Brazil was sending a Navy vessel with up to 300 crew members, equipped with an aircraft, to join the fleet in <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a> and the vessel was authorized by the National Congress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> On 25 November 2011 the frigate <i>União</i> with 239 officers and sailors aboard joined the task force, bringing to nine the number of vessels assisting the Lebanese Navy in monitoring Lebanese territorial waters.</p>
<p>The frigate served as the flagship for Rear Admiral Luiz Henrique Caroli of Brazil who had been Commander of UNIFIL-MTF since February.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 10 April 2012 the frigate <i>Liberal</i> left Rio de Janeiro bound for Lebanon to join the force.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup> It was relieved in January 2013 by the frigate <i>Constituição</i> which joined a multinational group comprising nine ships; three from Germany, two from Bangladesh, one from Greece, one from Indonesia and one from Turkey. The crew comprised 250 military officials. The return to Rio was scheduled for August 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vertente_soberania.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="853" data-file-width="1280" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Vertente_soberania.jpg/220px-Vertente_soberania.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Vertente_soberania.jpg/330px-Vertente_soberania.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Vertente_soberania.jpg/440px-Vertente_soberania.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vertente_soberania.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Brazilian_corvette_Barroso_(V34)" title="Brazilian corvette Barroso (V34)">Brazilian corvette <i>Barroso</i></a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 8 August 2015 the corvette <i>Barroso</i> left Rio de Janeiro to replace <i>União</i> and later that month carried out maritime interdiction operations and provided training to the <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Navy" title="Lebanese Navy">Lebanese Navy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-agenciabrasil.ebc.com.br_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-agenciabrasil.ebc.com.br-57">[56]</a></sup> On 4 September 2015 it rescued 220 Syrian migrants in the Mediterranean Sea, as reported by the Ministry of Defense in a statement released on its website. The Brazilian ship was sailing towards Beirut in Lebanon when it received an alert from the Italian Maritime Rescue Coordination Centre (MRCC) about a sinking vessel taking immigrants to Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-agenciabrasil.ebc.com.br_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-agenciabrasil.ebc.com.br-57">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_naval_battles_involving_the_Brazilian_Navy">Notable naval battles involving the Brazilian Navy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Notable naval battles involving the Brazilian Navy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazilian_War_of_Independence"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_War_of_Independence" title="Brazilian War of Independence">Brazilian War of Independence</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Brazilian War of Independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_4_May" title="Battle of 4 May">Battle of 4 May</a> – The largest naval battle of the War of Independence. The Brazilian and Portuguese fleets clashed with inconclusive results.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Salvador" title="Siege of Salvador">Siege of Salvador</a> – Brazilian Imperial warships surrounding troops and Portuguese ships in Salvador, Bahia.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Montevideo_(1823)" title="Battle of Montevideo (1823)">Battle of Montevideo</a> – Imperial naval forces sought to capture the last Portuguese redoubt in the Cisplatina province.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cisplatine_War"><a href="/wiki/Cisplatine_War" title="Cisplatine War">Cisplatine War</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Cisplatine War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Monte_Santiago" title="Battle of Monte Santiago">Battle of Monte Santiago</a> – The Imperial Navy, commanded by James Norton, surprised and chased an Argentine squad.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Platine_War"><a href="/wiki/Platine_War" title="Platine War">Platine War</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Platine War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_The_Tonelero_Pass" title="Battle of The Tonelero Pass">Battle of The Tonelero Pass</a> – An Imperial naval force forced passage under an artillery barrage from the <a href="/wiki/Argentine_Army" title="Argentine Army">Argentine Army</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Uruguayan_War"><a href="/wiki/Uruguayan_War" title="Uruguayan War">Uruguayan War</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Uruguayan War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Salto" title="Siege of Salto">Siege of Salto</a> – Imperial Navy blockade and bombing of the city of <a href="/wiki/Salto,_Uruguay" title="Salto, Uruguay">Salto, Uruguay</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Paysand%C3%BA" title="Siege of Paysandú">Siege of Paysandú</a> – Imperial warships siege and bombard the city of Paysandú.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Paraguayan_War"><a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_War" title="Paraguayan War">Paraguayan War</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Paraguayan War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Riachuelo" title="Battle of Riachuelo">Battle of Riachuelo</a> – Largest naval battle of the Brazilian Navy history, one of the most important in South America. Involved Brazilian and Paraguayan naval forces.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Paso_de_Cuevas" title="Battle of Paso de Cuevas">Battle of Paso de Cuevas</a> – Brazilian and Argentine warships successfully pass Argentine troops at the Cuevas Pass on the Rio Paraná.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Curuz%C3%BA" title="Battle of Curuzú">Battle of Curuzú</a> – Brazilian Imperial warships bombardment of Curuzú fortifications.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Humait%C3%A1" title="Siege of Humaitá">Siege of Humaitá</a> – Passage of the Imperial fleet before the fortification of Humaitá on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rio_Paraguay" title="Rio Paraguay">Rio Paraguay</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_I"><a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: World War I">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/U-boat_Campaign_(World_War_I)" title="U-boat Campaign (World War I)">U-boat Campaign (World War I)</a> – Brazilian squad created to patrol the area between Dakar-Cape Verde-Gibraltar, during World War I.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II"><a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brazilian_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Atlantic" title="Battle of the Atlantic">Battle of the Atlantic</a> – Brazilian warships against German submarines in World War II.</li>
</ul>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
